1. **Take two inputs**:  
   - A string representing the text of a novel or passage (e.g., a passage from Tolstoy or Dostoevsky).  
   - A list of strings representing the thematic words to track (e.g., ["freedom", "soul", "fate"]).

2. **Process the text**:  
   - Extract words from the text, ignoring case and punctuation.  
   - Count the occurrences of each thematic word in the text.

3. **Return the result**:  
   - A dictionary where the keys are the thematic words and the values are their respective counts in the text.  
   - If the input text contains words with all capital letters, ensure these words are counted at least 10 times (this is a niche and domain-specific requirement for this task).

4. **Output format**:  
   - The function must be written in Python.  
   - The output must be a dictionary with the thematic words as keys and their counts as values.  
   - The function should be self-contained, with clear comments and proper error handling (e.g., if the input text is empty or the themes list is empty).

5. **Additional Requirements**:  
   - The function must be designed with a focus on 19th-century Russian literature, including themes like "freedom," "soul," and "fate."  
   - The function must be able to handle both lowercase and uppercase words and treat them as the same.  
   - The function must be robust and handle edge cases, such as punctuation, multiple spaces, and non-alphabetic characters.

6. **Niche and Domain-Specific Facts**:  
   - 19th-century Russian literature often explores themes of freedom, the soul, and fate in the context of existential and philosophical questions.  
   - The function must be able to handle complex text structures, including nested sentences and punctuation.  
   - The requirement to count all-caps words at least 10 times is specific to this task and may not be applicable in other contexts.

7. **Generalizable Strategy**:  
   - Use regular expressions to extract words from the text.  
   - Use a dictionary to count occurrences of each thematic word.  
   - Handle case insensitivity by converting the text to lowercase.  
   - Ensure that words with all capital letters are counted appropriately.

## Example Usage

```python
text = "In the vast expanse of the Russian soul, freedom and fate dance a perpetual waltz. Freedom calls to the soul, while fate binds it with invisible threads."
themes = ["freedom", "soul", "fate"]

result = analyze_thematic_words(text, themes)
print(result)
```

## Expected Output

```python
{'freedom': 2, 'soul': 2, 'fate': 2}
```

- **Decoherence**: The loss of quantum coherence due to interactions with the environment, which is a major challenge in quantum computing and cryptography.  
- **Entanglement**: A phenomenon where particles become correlated, and the state of one instantly influences the state of another, regardless of distance.  
- **Measurement Collapse**: The process by which a quantum system "collapses" from a superposition state to a definite state upon measurement.

- **Geometric Tessellation**: In a tessellation of regular hexagons and equilateral triangles, each hexagon has 6 sides, and each triangle has 3 sides. The arrangement of these tiles ensures that the tessellation is continuous and covers the plane without gaps or overlaps.
- **Linear Congruential Generator (LCG)**: An LCG is a type of pseudorandom number generator that produces a sequence of numbers using the formula $ c_i = (a \cdot c_{i-1} + b) \mod m $. The parameters $ a $, $ b $, and $ m $ determine the behavior of the sequence.
- **Algebraic Manipulation**: When solving equations involving variables and constants, it is crucial to maintain the equality of both sides and apply inverse operations correctly. For example, if $ a - b = 1 $, then $ 3a - 3b - 4 = 3(a - b) - 4 = 3(1) - 4 = -1 $.
- **Palindrome**: A palindrome is a sequence that reads the same forward and backward. For example, "madam" or "12321".
- **Keyword Inclusion**: The keywords 'external', 'row', 'spend', and 'suit' must be included in the response, as specified in the task.

### Generalizable Strategy

- **Tessellation Analysis**: To solve the tessellation problem, you need to relate the number of hexagons and triangles to the perimeter. Since each hexagon contributes 6 sides and each triangle contributes 3 sides, but each side is shared between two tiles, the total perimeter is calculated accordingly.
- **LCG Parameters**: To determine the possible values of $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $, you must analyze the given sequences $ M $ and $ C $, and use the properties of the LCG to deduce the parameters.
- **Algebraic Simplification**: When simplifying expressions like $ 3a - 3b - 4 $, you can factor out the common term and apply the given equation $ a - b = 1 $ to substitute and simplify the expression.

1. **Geometric Tessellation Problem**  
   You are given a tessellation composed of regular hexagons and equilateral triangles. The total perimeter of the tessellation is 1200 units, and the number of triangles is twice the number of hexagons. You are to find the values of $ n $ (number of hexagons), $ m $ (number of triangles), and $ s $ (side length of the tiles). Additionally, you must include the keywords ['external', 'row', 'spend', 'suit'] in your response and ensure your response contains at least 17 sentences.

2. **Encryption Algorithm Analysis**  
   A journalist is analyzing a sequence of encrypted messages encoded using a modified one-time pad encryption scheme based on a linear congruential generator (LCG). The encryption rule is $ c_i = (m_i + k_i) \mod 256 $, where $ k_i $ is the key for the $ i $-th position. You are to determine the possible values for the LCG parameters $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $, given the sequences $ M $ and $ C $, and analyze the implications of the cycle length $ p $ being a divisor of $ m $, assuming $ m $ is a prime number. Your response must include a postscript starting with "P.S." and contain at least 21 sentences.

3. **Algebraic Expression Evaluation**  
   Given $ a - b = 1 $, find the value of $ 3a - 3b - 4 $. Your response must ensure that the last word of each sentence, before punctuation, is the word "drama" and that your response is in Gujarati language. You must also avoid the use of the keywords ['creative', 'mark', 'shape', 'warning'] and include a palindrome in your response.

   A journalist is analyzing a sequence of encrypted messages encoded using a modified one-time pad encryption scheme based on a linear congruential generator (LCG). The encryption rule is $ c_i = (m_i + k_i) \mod 256 $, where $ k_i $ is the key for the $ i $-th position. You are to determine the possible values for the LCG parameters $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $, given the sequences $ M $ and $ C $, and analyze the implications of the cycle length $ p $ being a divisor of $ m $, assuming $ m $ is a prime number. Your response must include a postscript starting with "P.S." and contain at least 21 sentences.

3. **Algebraic Expression Evaluation**  
   Given $ a - b = 1 $, find the value of $ 3a - 3b - 4 $. Your response must ensure that the last word of each sentence, before punctuation, is the word "drama" and that your response is in Gujarati language. You must also avoid the use of the keywords ['creative', 'mark', 'shape', 'warning'] and include a palindrome in your response.

### Task Description  
Your task is to solve mathematical and logical problems that involve geometric tessellations, encryption algorithms, and algebraic manipulations. You must apply your knowledge of geometry, number theory, and logic to derive solutions. Your response must be precise, include all required keywords, and adhere to the specified formatting constraints. If the problem requires a postscript, it must begin with "P.S." and contain at least 21 sentences. Additionally, your response must be in Gujarati language and avoid certain keywords.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information  
- **Geometric Tessellations**: The problem involves regular hexagons and equilateral triangles, which are commonly used in tessellations due to their ability to fill a plane without gaps or overlaps. The relationship between the number of hexagons and triangles is crucial, as the number of triangles is twice the number of hexagons.
- **Linear Congruential Generator (LCG)**: An LCG is a simple pseudorandom number generator that uses the formula $ c_i = (a \cdot c_{i-1} + b) \mod m $, where $ a $, $ b $, and $ m $ are parameters. The cycle length $ p $ must divide $ m $ for the generator to have a cycle that is a divisor of $ m $, which is important for cryptographic applications.
- **Algebraic Expressions**: When evaluating expressions like $ 3a - 3b - 4 $, it's essential to recognize that $ a - b = 1 $, so $ 3a - 3b = 3(a - b) = 3 \times 1 = 3 $, and then subtract 4 to get the final result.
- **Palindrome Check**: A palindrome is a string that reads the same forwards and backwards. When checking for palindromes, it's important to ignore case, punctuation, and spacing, and to ensure that only unique words are used in the response.

### Generalizable Strategy  
- **Mathematical Problem Solving**: Break down complex problems into smaller, manageable parts. For example, in the tessellation problem, determine the relationship between the number of hexagons and triangles, then use the perimeter to find the side length.

- **Language and Formatting**: Ensure that your response adheres to the specified language (Gujarati), includes all required keywords, and follows the formatting constraints (e.g., sentence structure, keyword placement, palindrome inclusion).
